Ruling for Istihada: Wudu for Each Prayer Time
Ruling with proof: istihada does not prevent worship, and wudu is required per prayer time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for wudu for a mustahada, explain the proof from the hadith, and apply the rule to different prayer times.

Core Idea
A mustahada performs wudu once per prayer time; bleeding does not break it within that time.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah clarifies how istihada (chronic bleeding) interacts with worship. While hayd prevents prayer and fasting, istihada does not. The key issue is wudu: how often must a mustahada renew it? The commentator explains the ruling based on the hadith and clarifies the condition for the excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The author states that istihada does not prevent prayer, fasting, or cutting (i.e., the cessation of hayd). This means worship is valid despite ongoing bleeding. The commentator affirms this ruling.
2
Locate the evidence
The commentator cites the hadith: 'Avoid prayer during your hayd days, then bathe, pray, and perform wudu for every prayer.' This is the proof that istihada does not prevent prayer, and that wudu is required.
The hadith also permits marital relations with a mustahada.
3
Analyze the wording for wudu frequency
The hadith says 'for every prayer' (li-kulli salat). The Hanafi school interprets this as per each prayer time, not for every individual prayer. The commentator explicitly says 'for the time of each obligatory prayer' (li-waqti kulli fard).
One wudu suffices for multiple prayers within the same time period.
4
Understand the condition for the excuse
The mustahada is excused because her hadath (state of impurity) occurs at every prayer time. It does not need to fill the entire time; it suffices that it is present at some point in each time.
This is what the commentator means by 'occurring at every time of the obligatory prayer, even if for an hour.'
5
Note the applications
The same wudu rule applies for supererogatory prayers (like Eid, Duha) and even for touching the mus-haf outside prayer times. The commentator adds these from al-Harawi.

[1] His saying: 'khabarah'—the fa entered it because the mubtada includes the meaning of a condition. [2] His saying: 'la tamna' salat'—based on the hadith: 'Avoid prayer during your hayd days, then bathe, pray, and perform wudu for every prayer.' And in one narration: 'Even if blood drips on the mat.' Recorded by Abu Dawud, Ahmad, Ibn Majah, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, al-Bazzar, Ibn Abi Shayba, and others. And in Sunan Abi Dawud: Umm Habish bint Jahsh was a mustahada, and her husband used to have intercourse with her. [3] His saying: 'wa man lam yamdi'—i.e., one for whom no time of obligatory prayer passes except that he has the hadath he is afflicted with, not meaning that the hadath fills the entire time, for that is not a condition for the excuse; rather, it means that it occurs at every time of the obligatory prayer, even if for an hour of it. [4] His saying: 'li-waqti kulli fard'—even if there is no interval between the two times. Similarly, he performs wudu for the time of Eid prayer, the time of Duha prayer, and for touching the mus-haf outside the prayer time. Thus said the commentator al-Harawi. And similar in Sunan al-Darimi (1:224), al-Mustadrak (4:69), Sunan al-Tirmidhi (1:221), and Sunan Abi Dawud (1:132), etc.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the matn's ruling regarding istihada. It explains the grammatical point about the fa in 'fahuwa istihada'. Then it provides the proof for the ruling that istihada does not prevent prayer: the hadith instructing the mustahada to avoid prayer during her hayd days, then bathe, pray, and perform wudu for every prayer, even if blood drips on the mat. The commentator then clarifies the condition for wudu: it is for the time of each obligatory prayer, not that the hadath must fill the entire time; it suffices that the hadath occurs at each prayer time. This also applies to supererogatory prayers performed following the obligatory one. The hadith also allows the husband to have intercourse with a mustahada. The commentator also notes exceptions: wudu is also required for Eid prayer, Duha prayer, and even for touching the mus-haf outside prayer times. The passage concludes with multiple hadith citations supporting the rule that the mustahada performs wudu for each prayer.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihada): Chronic bleeding from a vein that is not hayd; it has its own rulings.
حدث (hadath): A state of ritual impurity that normally invalidates wudu, but due to continual nature, a special dispensation is given.
مستحاضة (mustahada): A woman experiencing istihada (chronic non-menstrual bleeding).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) For every single prayer

The Wudu of the Ma'dhur: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Its Nullification
Expansion of the ruling on istihadah and the intra-Hanafi dispute on the naqid of wudu for a ma'dhur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the nullification of wudu for a ma'dhur, explain the proofs of the three positions (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, Zufar, Abu Yusuf), and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
A ma'dhur's wudu lasts the entire fard time; only its exit nullifies—entry does not.

This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi debate: what nullifies the wudu of a person with a chronic excuse (ma'dhur) such as istihadah? The source text expands the ruling from the matn and presents the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute sharpens your grasp of how the Hanafi school derives rulings for continuous events.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ma'dhur and his ruling
Who is a ma'dhur? What is the basic ruling on his wudu? The ma'dhur is someone who never experiences a moment free from a continuous hadath (e.g., istihadah, nosebleed). He must perform wudu for the time of each obligatory prayer.
2
Understand the three positions
State the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf regarding what nullifies the wudu. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: only exit of time nullifies. Zufar: only entry of time nullifies. Abu Yusuf: both entry and exit nullify.
3
Examine the proofs
What hadith does Abu Hanifa cite? The Prophet (peace be upon him) told a mustahadah: 'Then perform wudu for every prayer until that time comes.' This indicates the wudu is valid for the entire time. What logical arguments do Zufar and Abu Yusuf make? Zufar: no need before time, so wudu cannot be valid before entry. Abu Yusuf: need is only during the time, so wudu is not valid outside the time, hence both entry and exit are conflicting.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the text rebut the opposing views? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that the need exists for the entire time including its beginning; advancing wudu before time is a necessity to pray at the earliest moment. Exit of time signals the end of this need, causing the underlying event to take effect. The hadith explicitly states 'until that time comes', proving continuity throughout the time.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon and why? The view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the mufta bihi, as supported by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah. It balances practical ease with adherence to the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا تمنع صلاةً، وصوماً، وقطعاً، ومَن لم يمض عليه وقت فرض إلا وبه حدث من استحاضة، أو رعاف، أو نحوهما، يتوضأ لوقت كل فرض فقوله: وما نقص: مبتدأ، وقوله: فهو استحاضة: خبره. ثم بين حكم الاستحاضة، فقال: (لا تمنع صلاة، وصوماً، وقطعاً، ومَن لم يمض عليه وقت فرض إلا وبه حدث أي الحدث الذي ابتلي به، (من استحاضة، أو رعاف، أو نحوهما، يتوضأ لوقت كل فرض احتراز عن قول الشافعي فإن عنده يتوضأ لكل فرض)، ويصلي النوافل بتبعية الفرض. ويدل عليه ما ورد بروايات متعددة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم منع من وطء السبايا الحاملة حتى تضع، وعن وطء غير الحاملة حتى تستبرأ بحيضة وما ذلك إلا لتعرف براءة رحمها من الحمل، فجعل الحيض علامة البراءة، فعلم أن الحامل لا تحيض. ويصلي به فيه ما شاء من فرض ونفل، وينقضه خروج الوقت لا دخوله احتراز عن قول زفر له، فإن الناقض عنده دخول الوقت، وعن قول أبي يوسف له، فإن الناقض عنده كلاهما. ولنا: ما في صحيح البخاري إنه قال للمستحاضة: ثم توضئي لكل صلاة حتى يجي ذلك الوقت، فإنه صريح في أن الوضوء الواحد في الوقت كافٍ، وعلى هذا فيحمل اللام في الحديث السابق على الوقت أي لوقت كل صلاة، وفي المقام تفصيل مذكور في شرح المعاني الآثار للطحاوي وغيره. قوله: خروج الوقت؛ إسناد النقض إلى الخروج والدخول مجاز، فإن الناقض في هذه الصور هو الحدث السابق، وإنما ظهر أثره في هذا الوقت. قوله: دخول الوقت؛ لأن اعتبار الطهارة مع سيلان الحدث المنافي لها إنما هو للحاجة إلى الأداء، ولا حاجة قبل الوقت، فلا تعتبر، وبهذا استند أبو يوسف له، وزاد أن الحاجة مقصورة على الوقت لا قبله ولا بعده، فلا تعتبر الطهارة فيما عدا الوقت، فيكون الدخول والخروج كلاهما منافيين، فيعد كل منهما ناقضاً. ولأبي حنيفة ومحمد له أنه يحتاج إلى تقديم الطهارة على الوقت؛ ليتمكن من أداء الصلاة أول الوقت، وخروج الوقت دليل زوال الحاجة، فيظهر اعتبار الحدث عنده، والمراد بالوقت عندهما وقت الفريضة، فلو توضأ المعذور لصلاة العيد قبل الزوال له أن يصلي بذلك الوضوء الظهر، هو الصحيح. كذا في «الهداية».
It does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse. And whoever has not passed a time of obligatory prayer except that there is with him a type of chronic bleeding, or nosebleed, or the like, he performs wudu for the time of every obligatory prayer. His statement: 'and what is deficient' is the subject, and his statement: 'it is istihadah' is the predicate. Then he explained the ruling of istihadah and said: It does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse. And whoever has not passed a time of obligatory prayer except that there is with him an event (i.e. the event he is afflicted with), from istihadah, or nosebleed, or the like, he performs wudu for the time of every obligatory prayer, as a precaution against the statement of al-Shafi'i, for according to him he performs wudu for every prayer. And he prays supererogatory prayers following the obligatory. And it is indicated by what has been transmitted in multiple narrations that the Prophet, peace be upon him, prohibited intercourse with pregnant captives until they give birth, and with non-pregnant ones until they are cleared by one menstrual cycle, and that is only to know the purity of her womb from pregnancy, so he made menstruation a sign of purity, thus it is known that a pregnant woman does not menstruate. And he prays with it whatever he wishes of obligatory and supererogatory, and its nullification is the exit of the time, not its entry, as a precaution against the statement of Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, for according to him the invalidator is the entry of time, and against the statement of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, for according to him the invalidator is both. And we have: what is in Sahih al-Bukhari that he said to the woman with chronic bleeding: 'Then perform wudu for every prayer until that time comes,' for it is explicit that one wudu is sufficient within the time, and upon this the 'lam' in the previous hadith is interpreted to mean 'for the time' i.e. for the time of every prayer, and in the context there is a detail mentioned in Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar by al-Tahawi and others. His statement: 'exit of time'; attributing nullification to exit and entry is metaphorical, for the invalidator in these cases is the previous event, but its effect appears at this time. His statement: 'entry of time'; because the consideration of purity while the conflicting event is flowing is only due to the need for performance, and there is no need before the time, so it is not considered, and upon this Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, relied, adding that the need is confined to the time, not before or after, so purity is not considered outside the time, thus both entry and exit are conflicting, so each is considered an invalidator. And for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, he needs to advance the purity before the time to be able to pray at the beginning of the time, and exit of time indicates the end of need, so the effect of the event appears at that point. And by 'time' according to them is meant the time of the obligatory prayer. So if the excused person performs wudu for the Eid prayer before noon, he may pray Dhuhr with that wudu – that is correct. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the ruling on istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding) and its implications for worship. The base matn states that istihadah does not prevent prayer, fasting, or marital relations. It then explains that a person who never experiences a moment free from this chronic flow (such as istihadah, nosebleed, etc.) must perform wudu for the time of each obligatory prayer. This is a concession to avoid hardship, contrasting with al-Shafi'i who requires a fresh wudu for each prayer. The commentator clarifies the definition: the phrase 'what is deficient' (ما نقص) refers to the blood that falls short of the minimum for hayd (menstruation), and 'it is istihadah' is the predicate. The passage then addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding what nullifies the wudu of such a person. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the wudu is nullified only by the exit of the fard time, not its entry. This is because they consider that the need for purity exists before the time to allow prayer at the earliest moment. Exit of time terminates that need, so the underlying event manifests as a nullification. Zufar holds that entry of time itself nullifies, reasoning that there is no need before the time. Abu Yusuf holds that both entry and exit nullify, as the need is only during the time. The passage cites a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed a mustahadah to do wudu for each prayer until the time comes, implying that one wudu suffices for the entire time. The commentator interprets the preposition 'li' (for) in the hadith as indicating 'for the time' rather than 'for each prayer'. This resolves the apparent conflict with the practice of performing multiple prayers with one wudu. The text also clarifies that if an excused person performs wudu for Eid prayer before noon, that wudu suffices for Dhuhr—this is the correct position as stated in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihadah): Chronic non-menstrual vaginal bleeding that continues beyond the normal period of hayd, or bleeding from a vein (istihadah) that does not prevent prayer or fasting.
معذور (ma'dhur): A person who is excused due to a continuous state of hadath (e.g., istihadah, urinary incontinence, continuous nosebleed) such that no time passes without the hadath; they are allowed to combine prayers with one wudu per fard time.
ناقض (naqid): An action or occurrence that nullifies wudu; for the ma'dhur, the dispute centers on whether entry of time, exit, or both act as the naqid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what nullifies the wudu of a ma'dhur (one with a chronic excuse)?
A) The entry of the time of the next obligatory prayer.
B) The exit of the time of the current obligatory prayer.
C) Both entry and exit of the time.
D) The occurrence of the chronic bleeding itself.

Key Takeaway
For a ma'dhur, the wudu performed for a fard time is nullified only by the exit of that time, not by its entry, according to the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Wudu Nullification for Mustahadah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains wudu validity for mustahadah and intra-Hanafi dispute on naqd factors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on when the wudu of a mustahadah is nullified, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute among Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to concrete scenarios.

Core Idea
Only exit of prayer time nullifies the wudu of a mustahadah – not entry, based on the hadith.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of wudu for a woman experiencing chronic uterine bleeding (mustahadah). While all Hanafi imams agree that her wudu can remain valid despite continuous bleeding, they differ on what event causes its nullification. The discussion revolves around the interpretation of a prophetic hadith and the underlying rationale of when purity is needed for prayer. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze textual evidence (dalil) and evaluate practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf) within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and context
Understand who the mustahadah is and why her wudu is a special case. She has continuous bleeding (istihadah) that does not prevent wudu validity, but the nullification becomes tied to prayer times.
2
State the positions of the four Hanafi imams
List what each imam considers as the nullifier: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad – only exit; Abu Yusuf – both entry and exit; Zufar – only entry.
3
Analyze the primary proof (dalil)
Examine the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari: 'then make wudu for every prayer until that time comes.' The word 'until' indicates continuity until the arrival of the next time, supporting that wudu lasts until the end of the current time (exit).
The lam in the hadith is interpreted as 'for the time' meaning the entire prayer time.
4
Understand the rational arguments
Abu Yusuf argues that purity is only needed during the prayer time itself, so both entry and exit are boundaries. Zufar says only entry because there is no need before the time. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad counter that one needs purity before the time to pray at its beginning, and exit signals the end of that need.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the dispute to concrete scenarios: if a mustahadah makes wudu before noon, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad she can pray until end of Zuhr; according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar, only before noon. Similarly for Fajr with wudu made after true dawn.
If wudu is made before true dawn, all agree it is not valid after sunrise, due to either exit (for three) or entry (for Zufar).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُصلى به فيه ما شاء من فرض ونفل، وينقضه خروج الوقت لا دخوله احتراز عن قول زفر، فإن الناقض عنده دخول الوقت، وعن قول أبي يوسف، فإن الناقض عنده كلاهما. ولنا: ما في صحيح البخاري أنه قال للمستحاضة: ثم توضئي لكل صلاة حتى يجي ذلك الوقت، فإنه صريح في أن الوضوء الواحد في الوقت كاف، وعلى هذا فيحمل اللام في الحديث السابق على الوقت أي لوقت كل صلاة. قوله: خروج الوقت؛ إسناد النقض إلى الخروج والدخول مجاز، فإن الناقض في هذه الصور هو الحدث السابق، وإنما ظهر أثره في هذا الوقت. قوله: دخول الوقت؛ لأن اعتبار الطهارة مع سيلان الحدث المنافي لها إنما هو للحاجة إلى الأداء، ولا حاجة قبل الوقت، فلا تعتبر، وبهذا استند أبو يوسف، وزاد أن الحاجة مقصورة على الوقت لا قبله ولا بعده، فلا تعتبر الطهارة فيما عدا الوقت، فيكون الدخول والخروج كلاهما منافيين، فيعد كل منهما ناقضاً. ولأبي حنيفة ومحمد أنه يحتاج إلى تقديم الطهارة على الوقت ليتمكن من أداء الصلاة أول الوقت، وخروج الوقت دليل زوال الحاجة، فيظهر اعتبار الحدث عنده، والمراد بالوقت عندهما وقت الفريضة، فلو توضأ المعذور لصلاة العيد قبل الزوال له أن يصلي بذلك الوضوء الظهر، هو الصحيح. كذا في الهداية. فيصلي به من توضأ قبل الزوال إلى آخر وقت الظهر لا بعد طلوع الشمس من توضأ قبله. [فصلي:] بيان لثمرة الخلاف، وحاصله: أن المعذور إذا توضأ قبل الزوال يجوز له أن يصلي بذلك الوضوء إلى آخر وقت الظهر عندهما، فإذا خرج وقت الظهر انتقض وضوؤه، وعند أبي يوسف وزفر لا يصلي به إلا قبل الزوال، وبعد الزوال لا لوجود دخول الوقت وهو ناقض عندهما. ولو توضأ معذور بعد طلوع الفجر وقبل طلوع الشمس يجوز له أن يصلي به ما شاء قبل طلوع الشمس وبعده لا عندهما لوجود خروج وقت الصبح الناقض، وكذا عند أبي يوسف لأن الخروج عنده أيضاً ناقض، ويجوز عند زفر لأنه لم يوجد الدخول الناقض. [قوله: لكن...] لما كان قول المصنف: من توضأ قبله أعم من أن يتوضأ بعد طلوع الصبح الصادق أو فيما بينه وبين طلوع الشمس مع أن الخلاف يظهر في الصورة الأولى قيده به، فإنه لو توضأ قبل طلوع الصبح الصادق لا يجوز به أداء الصلاة بعد طلوع الشمس اتفاقاً، فعند الأئمة الثلاثة لوجود الخروج، وعند زفر لوجود دخول وقت صلاة الفجر.
He may pray with it whatever he wishes of obligatory and supererogatory prayers, and its nullification is by the exit of the time, not by its entry, as a safeguard against the saying of Zufar, for the nullifier according to him is the entry of the time, and against the saying of Abu Yusuf, for the nullifier according to him is both. Our proof is what is in Sahih al-Bukhari that he said to the mustahadah: 'Then make wudu for every prayer until that time comes.' It is explicit that one wudu suffices for the time. Based on this, the lam in the previous hadith is interpreted to mean 'for the time' i.e., for the time of each prayer. [Commentary: 'Exit of the time'; attributing nullification to exit and entry is metaphorical, for the nullifier in these cases is the previous hadath, but its effect appears only in that time. 'Entry of the time'; because the consideration of purity with the continuous flow of the hadath contrary to it is only for the need to perform, and there is no need before the time, so it is not considered. Abu Yusuf used this as his basis, and added that the need is confined to the time, not before or after, so purity is not considered outside the time, thus both entry and exit are contrary, hence each is considered a nullifier. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he needs to perform purity before the time to be able to pray at the beginning of the time, and exit of the time is evidence of the end of the need, so the hadath is considered effective then. By 'time' according to them is meant the time of the obligatory prayer. So if a person with an excuse makes wudu for Eid prayer before noon, he may pray Zuhr with that wudu; this is correct. As in al-Hidayah. He may pray with it from one who made wudu before noon until the end of Zuhr time, but not after sunrise from one who made wudu before it. [Fasalli:] Explanation of the practical consequence of the dispute; its gist is that if the excused person makes wudu before noon, he may pray with that wudu until the end of Zuhr time according to them, then when Zuhr time exits, his wudu is nullified. According to Abu Yusuf and Zufar, he may only pray with it before noon, and after noon no, because of the entry of the time which is a nullifier according to them. If an excused person makes wudu after dawn (true dawn) and before sunrise, he may pray with it whatever he wishes before sunrise, but after sunrise no according to them, because of the exit of the Fajr time which is a nullifier; similarly according to Abu Yusuf because exit is also a nullifier according to him; and according to Zufar it is permissible because no entry of the nullifier has occurred. [His saying: 'but...'] Since the author's statement 'who made wudu before it' is general, including whether he made wudu after true dawn or between that and sunrise, while the dispute appears in the first case, he [the commentator] qualified it accordingly. For if he made wudu before true dawn, he may not perform prayer with it after sunrise unanimously; according to the three imams due to exit, and according to Zufar due to the entry of Fajr prayer time.
Source pages p. 541

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about when the wudu of a mustahadah (woman with chronic uterine bleeding) is nullified. The base text states that exit of the prayer time breaks wudu, not entry, to differentiate from Zufar (who says entry breaks) and Abu Yusuf (who says both break). The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'then make wudu for every prayer until that time comes', meaning one wudu suffices for the entire prayer time. The commentator explains that attributing nullification to time is metaphorical; the actual nullifier is the continuous hadath, but its effect appears only at certain times. Abu Yusuf argues that since purity is only needed for prayer performance, and the need is limited to the time itself, both entry and exit mark boundaries where the hadath becomes effective. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad counter that one needs to be pure before the time to pray at its beginning, and exit signals the end of that need. The term 'time' refers to the obligatory prayer time. The practical consequence (thamarah) is illustrated: if a mustahadah makes wudu before noon, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad she can pray until the end of Zuhr; according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar, only before noon. Similarly, if she makes wudu after true dawn, she can pray until sunrise according to Hanifa and Muhammad, but not after, while Zufar allows it because entry of Fajr time (the nullifier for him) has not yet occurred. The commentator also notes that if wudu is made before true dawn, all agree it is not valid after sunrise, because exit (for three) or entry (for Zufar) has occurred. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as stated in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman with chronic uterine bleeding (istihadah) that is not menstrual.
الناقض (al-naqid): That which nullifies wudu; here expanded to include time-boundary events like entry or exit of prayer time.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamaratu al-khilaf): The practical consequence arising from a juristic disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what nullifies the wudu of a mustahadah?
A) The entry of the prayer time
B) The exit of the prayer time
C) Both entry and exit
D) Neither entry nor exit

Key Takeaway
The wudu of a mustahadah remains valid until the exit of the current prayer time, based on the hadith and the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Definition of Nifas (Postpartum Bleeding)
Defines nifas linguistically and legally with a condition for Cesarean cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal definition of nifas and identify the condition that distinguishes it from other postpartum bleeding.

Core Idea
Postpartum bleeding is nifas only if it exits the uterus via the vagina after childbirth or after most of the child emerges.

Nifas, or postpartum bleeding, is a critical category in taharah (purification). This passage defines it both linguistically and legally, establishing a precise condition: the blood must come from the uterus through the vaginal canal after childbirth. An important edge case—Cesarean delivery—clarifies that surgical bleeding does not count as nifas.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the linguistic meaning
The term 'nifas' in language means childbirth itself. Note that this is broader than the legal meaning.
2
Extract the legal definition
The legal (shar'i) definition specifies blood exiting from the uterus via the front (vagina) after the child leaves or after most of the child emerges.
The phrase 'أو أكثره' (or most of it) covers partial delivery.
3
Identify the condition (shart)
The blood must be from the uterus and exit through the vagina. This excludes bleeding from other sources like a Cesarean wound.
This condition is crucial to distinguish nifas from irregular bleeding (istihada).
4
Apply to the Cesarean edge case
If delivery is via the navel (Cesarean), nifas applies only if blood flows from the uterus vaginally. Otherwise, no nifas.
This shows that the mode of delivery does not determine nifas; the source of blood does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنفاس هو بالكسر والفتح، لغة: الولادة، وشرعاً: عبارة عن دم خارج من الرحم من القبل عقب خروج ولد أو أكثره، فلو ولدته من السرة فإن سال الدم من الرحم من القبل فنفساء، وإلا لا.
An-Nifas, with kasra or fatha on the nun, linguistically means childbirth, and legally is blood exiting from the uterus from the front following the exit of a child or most of it. If she gave birth from the navel (i.e., Cesarean), then if blood flows from the uterus from the front, she is nafsa (in postpartum bleeding); otherwise no.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a definition of nifas (postpartum bleeding). It begins with the linguistic meaning: 'nifas' means childbirth. Then it gives the legal (shar'i) definition: blood that exits from the uterus (specifically from the front, meaning vaginal canal) after the birth of a child, or after the majority of the child has emerged. The phrase 'or most of it' (أو أكثره) indicates that if most of the child has been delivered, the bleeding that occurs after that is considered nifas. Then it clarifies an edge case: if the child is delivered via Cesarean (from the navel), then nifas applies only if blood actually flows from the vaginal canal; otherwise, if no such blood appears, she is not considered a nafsa (woman in postpartum state). This distinguishes nifas from surgical bleeding. The commentator notes that the author's definition has a clear flaw (خلل بينا), presumably because it may not cover all conditions or may be imprecise, but the passage provides the standard definition.

Key Terms
النفاس (an-nifas): Blood exiting from the uterus via the vagina after childbirth or after most of the child has emerged.
النفساء (an-nafsa'): A woman who is experiencing postpartum bleeding (nifas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nifas is legally defined as vaginal blood following childbirth or after most of the child's emergence; if no such blood, she is not nafsa.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Invalidator of the Ma‘dhūr’s Wudu
Explaining the thamarah of ikhtilaf on the naqid for the ma'dhur's wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on what invalidates the ma‘dhūr’s wudu, identify the mufta bihi view, and apply the thamarah in scenarios.

Core Idea
For the ma‘dhūr, exit of prayer time (not entry) invalidates wudu according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This lesson unpacks a famous intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: what exactly breaks the wudu of a person with a chronic excuse (ma‘dhūr)? Is it the entry of a new prayer time, the exit of the current one, or both? The answer determines exactly when the ma‘dhūr must renew wudu. We will trace the three positions through the thamarah (practical consequence) as explained in the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions on the invalidator
From the passage, extract what each of the four imams (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, Zufar) considers the nāqiḍ (invalidator) of the ma‘dhūr’s wudu. Note that Abu Yusuf accepts both entry and exit.
This is the core ikhtilaf – each imam has a distinct view.
2
Trace the thamarah for the first scenario
The author gives the example of a ma‘dhūr who performs wudu before noon (i.e., during Dhuhr time). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he may pray until the end of Dhuhr time; according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar, he cannot pray after noon because entry of Asr time invalidates the wudu (for them).
Abu Yusuf and Zufar both consider entry as nāqiḍ, but Abu Yusuf agrees the exit also invalidates.
3
Trace the thamarah for the second scenario
The ma‘dhūr performs wudu after true dawn (Fajr) but before sunrise. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, he may pray until sunrise (exit of Fajr time). According to Abu Yusuf, same result because exit invalidates. According to Zufar, he may pray even after sunrise because the entry that would invalidate (of the next prayer) has not yet occurred.
This shows Zufar’s view leads to a different practical outcome in this case.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The author indicates that the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). This is the view that only the exit of the current prayer time invalidates the ma‘dhūr’s wudu.
This is the established ruling of the school despite intra-school disagreement.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a new case (e.g., ma‘dhūr performs wudu in the middle of Asr time), determine until when he can pray with that wudu according to each view, and state the mufta bihi ruling.
This reinforces the practical application.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So he prays with it (the wudu) whoever performed wudu before noon until the end of the time of Dhuhr, not after sunrise from one who performed wudu before it. And nifas is blood... [1] [2] He says: 'So he prays with it whoever performed wudu before noon until the end of the time of Dhuhr' — contrary to Abu Yusuf, because for him the entry of time occurred, not the exit. (Not after sunrise from one who performed wudu before it): meaning whoever performed wudu before sunrise but after dawn, contrary to Zufar, because for him the invalidator exists in our view and Abu Yusuf's, which is the exit, not in Zufar's view, because for him the invalidator is the entry, and it did not occur. And nifas is blood... [1] His statement: 'So he prays' is an explanation of the fruit of the dispute. Its gist is that the ma'dhur, if he performed wudu before noon, is allowed to pray with that wudu until the end of Dhuhr time according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). When Dhuhr time exits, his wudu is invalidated. According to Abu Yusuf and Zufar, he cannot pray with it except before noon; after noon he cannot, because the entry of time occurred, which is the invalidator in their view. And if a ma'dhur performed wudu after dawn (i.e., true dawn) and before sunrise, he is allowed to pray with it whatever he wishes before sunrise; after sunrise he cannot according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) due to the exit of dawn time which is the invalidator, and similarly according to Abu Yusuf because exit is also an invalidator in his view. But it is allowed according to Zufar because the entry (of the invalidator) did not occur. [2] His statement: 'But... etc.' Because the author's statement 'whoever performed wudu before it' is general, including whoever performed wudu after true dawn or in between that and sunrise, and since the dispute appears in the first scenario, he restricted it to that. So if he performed wudu before true dawn, it is not allowed to pray with it after sunrise by agreement — according to the three imams due to the occurrence of exit, and according to Zufar due to the occurrence of entry of the time of Fajr prayer.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute section explaining the practical consequence (thamarah) of the ikhtilaf regarding what invalidates the wudu of a ma'dhur (a person with a chronic excuse such as continuous bleeding). The author first presents the ruling: a ma'dhur who performs wudu before noon may pray with that wudu until the end of Dhuhr time according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). After Dhuhr time exits, the wudu is invalidated. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the entry of the time invalidates the wudu, so he cannot pray after noon. Similarly, for a ma'dhur who performs wudu after true dawn but before sunrise, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say he may pray before sunrise but not after sunrise, because the exit of Fajr time invalidates the wudu. Abu Yusuf agrees, since exit is an invalidator in his view. However, Zufar holds that only the entry of time invalidates, not the exit. Therefore, Zufar allows the ma'dhur to pray after sunrise in this scenario because the entry of the next time (but the next time entry? Actually, entry of Fajr time already occurred before the wudu? The text says 'because the entry did not occur' — meaning the entry of the time that would invalidate? The passage is a bit complex but the key is the identification of the naqid: for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad it is the exit of the prayer time, for Abu Yusuf it is both entry and exit (since he agreed with them on exit), and for Zufar it is only entry. The commentary also clarifies that if the ma'dhur performed wudu before true dawn, all agree he cannot pray after sunrise because the exit of the true dawn invalidates unanimously.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma‘dhūr): A person with a chronic excuse (e.g., continuous urine, istihada) that prevents wudu from lasting a full prayer time.
الناقض (al-nāqiḍ): What invalidates wudu. Here, the disagreed-upon cause: entry or exit of prayer time.
دخول الوقت (dukhūl al-waqt): The beginning of a new prayer time; considered an invalidator by Zufar and, partially, by Abu Yusuf.
خروج الوقت (khurūj al-waqt): The end of a prayer time; considered an invalidator by Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Muhammad
C) Abu Yusuf
D) Zufar

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that the ma‘dhūr’s wudu is invalidated by the exit of the current prayer time, not its entry.

Definition and Maximum Duration of Nifas
Defining nifas and stating its limits with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of nifas, identify that it has no minimum limit, and explain the evidence for the maximum of forty days.

Core Idea
Nifas has no minimum but a maximum of forty days, based on prophetic practice.

This lesson defines nifas (postpartum bleeding) and clarifies two key rulings: there is no minimum duration, and the maximum is forty days. Understanding these limits is essential for a woman to know when to resume prayer and fasting after childbirth. The Hanafi position is supported by hadith and contrasted with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its definition
Read the Arabic phrase 'والنفاسُ هو دَم يَعْقِبُ الولد' – nifas is blood that follows childbirth. Note that it begins after the child (or most of it) emerges.
Definition is key; it distinguishes nifas from other types of bleeding.
2
Understand the rulings on limits
The text states 'ولا حد لاقله' (no minimum) and 'أكثره أربعون يوماً' (maximum forty). Understand the consequence: if bleeding stops before forty days, she must perform ghusl and pray immediately.
The minimum is not defined; even a momentary bleed counts as nifas.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith of Umm Salama and Anas are cited. The Prophet's companions observed forty days, and the Prophet himself set that limit. The chain weaknesses are compensated by multiple paths, as verified by Ibn al-Humam.
The hadith is ahad but strengthened by multiple chains.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The text notes 'خلافاً للشافعي إذ أكثره ستون يوماً'. The Shafi'i school holds sixty days based on other evidence. Understand the practical difference: after forty days, Hanafis treat continued bleeding as istihada.
Thamarah al-khilaf: after forty days, Hanafi woman does ghusl and prays; Shafi'i woman waits up to sixty.
5
Summarize practical implication
A woman in nifas is exempt from prayer and fasting but must perform ghusl when bleeding stops. If bleeding exceeds forty days, she becomes mustahada (chronically bleeding) and must perform wudu for each prayer.
Knowing the maximum is crucial for correct practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنفاسُ هو دَم يَعْقِبُ الولد، ولا حد لاقله، وأكثره أربعون يوماً خلافاً للشَّافِعِي الله إذ أكثره ستون يوماً عنده. [ ۱ ] قوله : ولا حد ؛ أي ليس له حد شرعاً من الجانب الأقل، فلو رأت الدم ساعةً ثم طهرت يجب عليها أن تغتسل وتصلّي، وله حدّ من الجانب الآخر أخذا من حديث أم سلمة رضي الله عنها : «كانت النفساء تقعد على عهدِ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أربعين يوماً»(۲)، أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي، وعند الدارقطني وابن ماجه عن أنس: «وقت رسولُ الله للنفساء أربعين يوماً إلا أن ترى الطهر قبل ذلك»(۳)، وفي سنده " كلام ينجبر بكثرة الطرق كما حققه ابنُ الهمام في «فتح القدير» (٤)
And nifas is blood that follows the child, and there is no limit for its minimum, and its maximum is forty days — contrary to al-Shafi‘i, for its maximum according to him is sixty days. [1] His statement: 'There is no limit' means it has no legal limit on the lower side; so if she sees blood for an hour then becomes pure, she must perform ghusl and pray. And it has a limit on the other side, taken from the hadith of Umm Salama (may Allah be pleased with her): 'The women in nifas used to sit (abstain from prayer) for forty days during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him)' — narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi. And according to al-Daraqutni and Ibn Majah from Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah set forty days for the woman in nifas, unless she sees purity before that' — and its chain has some discussion that is compensated by numerous paths, as verified by Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling section on nifas (postpartum bleeding). The author first defines nifas as blood that follows childbirth (i.e., after the baby or most of it has emerged). Then he states two rulings: (1) There is no minimum limit for nifas — meaning if a woman bleeds for even a short time (like an hour) then stops, she must perform ghusl and pray; she does not wait for a minimum period. (2) The maximum limit is forty days. This is based on the practice of the Prophet's time reported in hadith of Umm Salama and Anas (may Allah be pleased with them). The author also notes that Imam al-Shafi‘i holds the maximum to be sixty days. The commentary explains that the hadiths supporting forty days, even if some have weakness in their chains, are strengthened by multiple narrations, as Ibn al-Humam verified. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that after forty days, if bleeding continues, it is considered istihada (chronic bleeding), not nifas, and she should perform ghusl and pray, and if bleeding persists, she should take wudu for each prayer.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifās): Blood that exits from the uterus following childbirth or when most of the child has emerged.
حد (ḥadd): A legal boundary; here, the minimum and maximum length of nifas.
أربعون يوماً (arba‘ūn yawman): Forty days — the agreed-upon maximum for nifas in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, nifas has no minimum duration, but its maximum is forty days, after which any continued bleeding is considered istihada.

Limits of Nifas: Minimum None, Maximum 40 Days
Ruling on nifas duration with hadith proof and Shafi'i disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of nifas, identify the supporting hadith evidence, and explain the point of disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Nifas has no minimum, but its maximum is 40 days; beyond that it is istihadah.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah addresses the duration of postpartum bleeding (nifas). The Hanafi school, relying on authentic hadith, sets no fixed minimum and a maximum of forty days. The Shafi'i school holds a different view, and the author explains the evidence and the practical implications of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act discussed is nifas (postpartum bleeding). The ruling is that it has no fixed minimum and a maximum of forty days.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Umm Salamah: 'The woman in nifas used to sit for forty days' and the hadith of Anas: 'The Prophet set the time as forty days.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The specific phrase 'arba'ina yawman' (forty days) indicates a fixed limit; the verb 'qa'ada' (sit) implies refraining from prayer, so the limit is for the period of prohibition.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds the maximum is sixty days. Their evidence includes other reports and qiyas with hayd.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi: after 40 days, blood is istihadah; Shafi'i: after 60 days. This affects when a woman must resume prayer and fasting.

Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement regarding nifas (postpartum bleeding). The author clarifies that nifas has no minimum duration—if a woman sees blood even for a moment and then becomes pure, she must perform ghusl and resume prayer. The maximum is forty days, based on the hadith of Umm Salamah and Anas (may Allah be pleased with them). The Shafi'i school holds the maximum to be sixty days. The Hanafi evidence is the authentic hadith and the practice of the Companions. The footnote discusses the ruling when only a part of the child emerges and the woman fears missing prayer: she must still pray by any means possible, even by gestures, and cannot delay the prayer. This underscores the extreme importance of prayer on time.

Key Terms
نفاس (nifās): Postpartum bleeding following childbirth
أربعون يوماً (arbaʿūna yawman): The maximum period of nifas according to the Hanafi school

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nifas has no set minimum duration; its maximum is forty days according to the Hanafi school, based on the hadith of Umm Salamah.

Rulings on Twins, Miscarriage, and Nifas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nifas with twins and rulings on miscarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nifas for twins, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply rulings of miscarriage (saqt) to nifas, umm walad, talaq, and 'iddah.

Core Idea
For twins, nifas begins with the first child; a miscarriage with visible limbs counts as a live birth for all major rulings.

This lesson examines a set of rulings connected by childbirth: the start of nifas for twins (with an intra-Hanafi disagreement), the completion of 'iddah, and the legal status of a miscarriage. Understanding these cases clarifies how the Hanafi school defines the beginning and end of nifas and the significance of a visible fetus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main issues
List the three distinct rulings covered: nifas for twins, saqt rulings, and 'iddah completion for twins.
2
Analyse the twin nifas dispute
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (nifas from first child) and the opposing view of Muhammad (nifas from second child). Examine their proofs: the opening of the cervix vs. continued pregnancy.
The practical difference: whether blood between births is nifas or not.
3
Examine the saqt rulings
Identify the condition for a miscarriage (saqt) to be considered a live birth: any limb visible. List the four consequences: nifas, umm walad, suspended talaq, and 'iddah completion.
4
Note the consensus on 'iddah for twins
Confirm that regardless of the nifas dispute, 'iddah ends with the birth of the last child by consensus, based on Quranic text.
5
Synthesize the combined principles
Understand how these rulings form a coherent framework: nifas begins with first birth event, but pregnancy continues until the last child is delivered, affecting 'iddah.

So she becomes in nifas due to it, and the slave-girl becomes umm walad. And the 'iddah is completed by it: i.e., if her husband divorces her, her 'iddah is completed by the emergence of this miscarriage. [1] His statement: 'and it is for the mother of twins...' means: she who gives birth to two children in one womb and between their births is less than six months, then her nifas is the blood that comes out after the first child according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), whereas according to Muhammad it is after the second child, based on the fact that before the second child she is pregnant, so she does not become in nifas. [2] His statement: 'and the completion...' means: if a pregnant woman is divorced or her husband dies, her 'iddah is completed by the birth of the second, not the first, by consensus, because the completion of 'iddah for a pregnant woman is by delivering the pregnancy and the uterus being empty, by the text of the Quran. And before the birth of the second, she is definitely pregnant, so the 'iddah is not completed. [3] His statement: 'and the slave-girl becomes umm walad': umm walad is a slave-girl whom her master had intercourse with, she gave birth to a child from him, and he claimed paternity; her ruling is that she becomes free after her master's death. So if a slave-girl gives birth to a miscarriage in which some limbs are apparent, she becomes umm walad if the master claims (paternity). (1) And the ruling is similar if she gives birth to three, with less than six months between the first and second, and similarly between second and third, but between first and third more than six months; then they are considered one pregnancy according to the correct view. See Hashiyah al-Shurnulali 'ala al-Durar (1:43). (2) Saqt: the kasrah (i) is more common: the child that falls from his mother's womb incomplete. See Taj al-Arus (19:356). (3) Al-Hidayah (1:192).
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings related to nifas, twins, and miscarriage (saqt). First, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a woman gives birth to twins with a gap of less than six months, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that nifas begins from the first child, because the cervix opens and blood flows. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that nifas begins from the second, as the woman is still pregnant after the first. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as given in al-Hidayah. Second, regarding 'iddah: if a pregnant woman is divorced or widowed, her 'iddah ends with the birth of the last child, by consensus, because the Quran states 'iddah is until delivery. Third, a saqt (miscarriage) in which some limbs (e.g., finger or hair) are visible is considered a live birth for rulings: the woman enters nifas, a slave-girl becomes umm walad if the master claims the child, a conditional divorce is triggered, and 'iddah is completed. The text also notes that if a woman gives birth to three children with intervals of less than six months but the overall duration exceeds six months, they are considered one pregnancy on the correct view.

Key Terms
توأمان (taw'amān): Two children from one womb, born with less than six months apart
سقط (saqṭ): A fetus that is born before full term, not fully developed
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A slave-woman who bears a child from her master, who claims paternity

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) From the first child
C) From neither, as nifas does not apply
D) From the last child regardless

Key Takeaway
For Hanafi fiqh, the beginning of nifas for twins is from the first child, and a miscarriage with visible limbs is treated as a live birth for key rulings.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Onset of Nifas for Twin Births and Rulings on Stillbirth
Expansion of the matn on nifas for twins and stillbirth rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when postpartum bleeding (nifas) begins for a woman delivering twins and explain the rulings on stillbirth in relation to nifas, umm walad, suspended divorce, and iddah.

Core Idea
Postpartum bleeding begins with the first twin; a stillbirth showing human features is legally a child.

The classical Hanafi texts address a nuanced dispute: when does a woman enter the state of nifas (postpartum bleeding) if she delivers twins? The majority view, held by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, holds that nifas begins with the first twin. Imam Muhammad disagrees, arguing that she remains pregnant until the second is born. This lesson unpacks that dispute and then extends the logic to stillbirths, showing that a miscarried fetus with discernible human features carries the same legal consequences as a live birth for nifas, umm walad, suspended divorce, and the waiting period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The matn states: 'وهو لأم التوأمين من الأول خلافاً لمحمد'. The student must recognize that the dispute is about whether nifas begins with the birth of the first twin or only after the second.
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold the first opinion; Muhammad holds the second.
2
Analyze the majority proof
The commentator explains: after the first birth, the mouth of the womb opens and blood flows, so the blood is necessarily nifas. This is based on physical reasoning (talil).
The proof is not a text but a necessary consequence of the physiological change.
3
Analyze the dissenting view and response
Muhammad argues that before the second birth she is still pregnant, so the blood cannot be nifas. The Hanafi response is that the opening of the cervix makes the blood nifas inevitably, regardless of the remaining twin.
The dissenting view is also based on a principle: nifas only occurs after complete delivery.
4
Examine the consensus on iddah
The passage notes that for a divorced or widowed pregnant woman, the waiting period ends only with the birth of the second twin, by consensus. This is because the iddah requires complete clearance of the womb.
This consensus shows that the nifas dispute does not affect iddah.
5
Apply the same definition to stillbirth
Understand that a stillbirth (siqt) that shows some human features (e.g., a hand or nail) is legally a 'child' (walad). Accordingly, it triggers nifas, makes a slave woman umm walad, triggers a suspended divorce, and ends the iddah.
The ruling applies only if the stillbirth exhibits discernible human features.

Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a ruling from the matn regarding postpartum bleeding (nifas) for a woman who delivers twins. The author clarifies that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two companions), the postpartum bleeding begins with the first twin, contrary to Muhammad al-Shaybani who holds that it begins only after the second twin. The reasoning for the majority view is that after the first birth, the cervix opens and blood flows, making the blood nifas invariably. Muhammad's position is that before the second birth, she is still pregnant, so the blood cannot be nifas. The passage then addresses three consequences: (1) completion of the waiting period (iddah) for a divorced or widowed pregnant woman, which by consensus ends only with the second twin; (2) if a stillbirth shows some human features (e.g., a hand or foot), it is legally considered a 'child' (walad) for the purposes of nifas, umm walad, and suspended divorce; and (3) the suspended divorce (ta'liq) is triggered by such a stillbirth. The author also defines twins as two children from one pregnancy with a gap of at least six months (the minimum pregnancy duration). The footnotes further clarify that umm walad status applies to a slave woman who delivers a stillbirth with discernible features, and that in case of triplets, if each pair is less than six months apart but the first and last are more than six months apart, they are considered one pregnancy.

Key Terms
توأم (taw'am): Two children born from one pregnancy (twins).
سقط (siqt): A stillbirth that shows some human features (e.g., a hand or nail).
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding following childbirth.
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who gives birth to her master's child, thereby gaining freedom upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Postpartum bleeding for twins begins with the first birth; a stillbirth with visible human features has the same legal effect as a live birth for nifas, umm walad, suspended divorce, and iddah.

Taharah — Purification

The Obligation to Purify the Body for Prayer
Definition and ruling on purification of the body for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying the body from physical impurities for prayer and explain why the declarative phrase is treated as a command indicating obligation.

Core Idea
Purifying the body from filth is wajib for prayer, because the mujtahid's statement carries the force of the Lawgiver.

This passage unpacks the opening phrase of the chapter on impurities. The commentator shows that 'yutahhiru' is structurally a statement but legally a command, obligating purification for prayer. He also clarifies that 'badan' means the torso, and that this obligation is specific to prayer—outside prayer, it is not required unless impurity exceeds a dirham. The lesson distinguishes this chapter from the later chapter on conditions of prayer, focusing here on the obligation itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic form
The word 'yutahhiru' is grammatically a declarative (khabar), but the commentator argues it is an imperative in meaning. Recognize this shift: in legal texts, a statement can have the force of a command.
This is a key hermeneutical principle: the mujtahid's statement runs in the course of the Lawgiver's statement in necessitating obligation.
2
Understand the juridical principle
The commentary cites al-Nihayah: the statement of the mujtahid is like the statement of the Lawgiver in creating obligation. Thus, the phrase 'yutahhiru' means 'it is obligatory to purify.'
This principle elevates the text from information to legal command.
3
Distinguish 'badan' from 'jasad'
The commentator clarifies that 'badan' (with two fathas) refers specifically to the torso (ما سوى الرأس والأطراف), while 'jasad' is the whole body. This affects the scope of purification: only the torso is the primary focus, though limbs are also covered by default.
This lexical precision avoids overextension.
4
Determine the scope of obligation
The attribution to 'the one praying' indicates that purification is obligatory only for prayer. Outside of prayer, it is not a duty unless the impurity exceeds a dirham and one has a pure garment available.
This limits the obligation to the act of prayer, not general cleanliness.
5
Differentiate from conditions of prayer
The commentator addresses why this chapter exists separately from the later chapter on conditions of prayer. Here the focus is the obligation (wajib) to purify, not whether it is a condition (shart) or pillar (rukn). That distinction belongs elsewhere.
This avoids redundancy and clarifies the purpose of each section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يَطْهُرُ بدنُ المصلِّي
( يَطْهُرُ بدنُ المصلّى )
[۲]
باب الأنجاس
باب الأنجاس
[ ١ ] قوله : يطهر ؛ بصيغة المجهول من التطهير، أو بصيغة المعروف من الطهارة ، والهاء على الأوّل مفتوحة وعلى الثاني مضمومة، وهو وإن كان خبراً صورة لكنه أمر معنى ؛ لما في «النهاية»: إنّ إخبار المجتهد يجري مجرى إخبار الشارع في اقتضاء الوجوب، بل هوا أكد من الأمر، فالمعنى يجب أن يطهر الأشياء المذكورة من النجاسات المذكورة، ويحتمل أن يكون الخبر على معناه ، ويكون المقصود الإخبار عما يطهر به الأشياء، وكيفية تطهيره شرعاً. [٢] قوله : بدن المصلي ؛ المراد بالبدن هاهنا الجسد، فإنّه صرح في «المغرب» و«مجمع البحار» وغيرهما : أنّ البَدَنَ بفتحتين اسم لما سوى الرأس والأطراف والجسد اسم للمجموع، وفي إضافته إلى المصلي إشارة إلى أنّ شرعية التطهير من النجاسات إنما لأداء الصلاة وما في حكمها. وإلى أنَّ الواجب إنَّما هو التطهير لمن يريد الصلاة، فأما خارج الصلاة فالتطهير ليس بفرض، فإنّه يجوزُ لبس الثوب النجس في غير الصلاة إلا إذا زادت النجاسة . ة على قدر الدرهم، وله ثوب طاهر كما صرح به في «القنية»، وفي المقام تفصيل ذكرناه في شرح باب شروط الصلاة من «السعاية»(۱).
هي
فإن قلت ما ذكره المصنف لوله هاهنا يغني عن قوله في «باب شروط الصلاة» :
هي تطهير بدن المصلّي من حدث وخبث وثوبه ومكانه»، فما وجه التكرار؟ قلت : لا غناء ولا تكرار، فإنّ المقصود هناك بيان أن طهارة البدن وغيره من الشرائط للصلاة، والغرض هاهنا مجرد وجوب تطهير البدن وغيره على المصلّي مع قطع النظر عن أن يكون فرضاً أو سنة، شرطاً أو ركناً.
(۱) «السعاية» (١ : ٥٦).
Pure is the body of the one praying. (Pure is the body of the one praying.) [2] Chapter of Impurities. Chapter of Impurities. [1] His statement: 'yutahhiru' (purifies) – in the passive form from tathir, or in the active form from taharah; the ha' on the first is fatha, on the second is damma. And although it is structurally a declarative sentence, it is an imperative in meaning; because in 'Al-Nihayah': 'Indeed the statement of the mujtahid runs in the course of the statement of the Lawgiver in necessitating obligation, nay it is stronger than the command.' So the meaning is: it is obligatory to purify the mentioned things from the mentioned impurities. And it is possible that the declarative is upon its meaning, and the purpose is to inform about what purifies things and how to purify them legally. [2] His statement: 'body of the one praying' – intended by 'badan' here is the torso, for it is stated in 'Al-Mughrib' and 'Majma' al-Bihar' and others that 'badan' (with two fathas) is a name for what is besides the head and limbs, and 'jasad' is a name for the whole. And in its attribution to the one praying, there is an indication that the legislation of purification from impurities is only for the performance of prayer and what is like it. And that the obligatory is only purification for the one who intends to pray; as for outside of prayer, purification is not a duty, for it is permissible to wear a impure garment outside of prayer unless the impurity exceeds the amount of a dirham, and he has a pure garment, as stated in 'Al-Qunyah'. And in this place there is a detail we have mentioned in the commentary on the chapter of conditions of prayer from 'Al-Si'ayah'. (1) 'If you say: what the author mentioned here dispenses with his statement in the Chapter of Conditions of Prayer: 'It is the purification of the body of the one praying from hadath and khabath and his garment and his place' – so what is the reason for repetition? I say: No dispensation and no repetition, for the purpose there is to show that purification of the body and other things are conditions for prayer, whereas the intent here is merely the obligation to purify the body and other things upon the one praying, regardless of whether it is fard or sunnah, condition or pillar.' (1) 'Al-Si'ayah' (1:56).
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on impurities (Bab al-Anjis). The author explains the phrase 'yutahhiru badan al-musalli' (pure is the body of the one praying) from the matn. He clarifies that the word 'yutahhiru' (it purifies) is grammatically a statement but legally a command, because the statement of a mujtahid has the force of the Lawgiver in obligating action. Thus, it means the worshiper must purify his body from the mentioned impurities. Then he defines 'badan' as the torso (excluding head and limbs), contrasting it with 'jasad' which covers the whole body. The attribution to the worshiper indicates that the obligation of purification is specifically for prayer; outside of prayer, purification is not obligatory unless the impurity exceeds a dirham's size and the person has a pure garment available. The author also addresses potential criticism about redundancy with another chapter (Conditions of Prayer). He distinguishes: there the focus is that purification is a condition of prayer; here the focus is the obligatory nature of purification itself, without confusing it with being a condition or pillar. This passage thus establishes that purification of the body from filth is a separate obligation for the one intending to pray, and it is not simply a condition but a wajib act.

Key Terms
بدن (badan): The torso, excluding the head and limbs (as opposed to jasad meaning the whole body).
النجاسة (al-najasah): Impurity (filth) on the body or garment that must be removed for prayer.
وجوب (wujub): Legal obligation (wajib) derived from the implied command of the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the specific meaning of 'badan' (body) in the phrase 'yutahhiru badan al-musalli'?
A) The entire body including head and limbs
B) The torso only, excluding the head and limbs
C) Only the private parts
D) The limbs used in prayer

Key Takeaway
Purifying the body from physical impurities is a distinct wajib act for prayer, derived from the implied command in the mujtahid's statement, and is not merely a condition.

Taharah — Purification

Purification from Visible Impurity: Ruling and Proofs
Expansion on purification obligation and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on purifying the body, clothes, and place from visible impurity for prayer, and identify the Quranic and prophetic proofs.

Core Idea
Purification from visible impurity is wajib for prayer, not outside prayer, established by Quran and explicit hadith.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqaya clarifies when and how a Muslim must purify from visible impurities. It distinguishes between obligation for prayer and permissibility outside prayer, and corrects a common misunderstanding that the proof for purifying the body and place is merely by indication. The commentator also defines what constitutes a visible impurity, which affects the method of purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that purification of the body, clothes, and place from impurities is wajib (obligatory) for the one who intends to pray. Outside prayer, it is not fard, though there are details.
The commentator explains that the verb 'yutahhar' is a report but functions as a command, indicating obligation.
2
Clarify the scope of obligation
The obligation is tied to prayer. Outside prayer, wearing an impure garment is permissible unless the impurity exceeds a dirham and one has a clean garment. This distinction is crucial for daily practice.
This addresses a potential redundancy with the chapter on conditions of prayer.
3
Locate the proofs
For clothes, the proof is the Quranic verse 'And your garments purify' (74:4). For body and place, some claim it is by indication (dalala), but the commentator insists explicit prophetic texts exist, as detailed in al-Si‘aya.
The commentator critiques al-Hidaya for relying on indication when direct hadith are available.
4
Understand the definition of visible impurity
A visible impurity (najas mar'i) is one that remains solid and congealed after drying, such as blood, stool, and semen. Non-visible impurities like urine are purified by washing without needing to remove a solid substance.
This categorization directly affects the method of purification.

Source Text

باب الأنجاس
[١] قوله : يطهر ; بصيغة المجهول من التطهير، أو بصيغة المعروف من الطهارة ، والهاء على الأوّل مفتوحة وعلى الثاني مضمومة، وهو وإن كان خبراً صورة لكنه أمر معنى ; لما في «النهاية»: إنّ إخبار المجتهد يجري مجرى إخبار الشارع في اقتضاء الوجوب، بل هو أكد من الأمر، فالمعنى يجب أن يطهر الأشياء المذكورة من النجاسات المذكورة، ويحتمل أن يكون الخبر على معناه ، ويكون المقصود الإخبار عما يطهر به الأشياء، وكيفية تطهيره شرعاً. [٢] قوله : بدن المصلي ; المراد بالبدن هاهنا الجسد، فإنّه صرح في «المغرب» و«مجمع البحار» وغيرهما : أنّ البَدَنَ بفتحتين اسم لما سوى الرأس والأطراف والجسد اسم للمجموع، وفي إضافته إلى المصلي إشارة إلى أنّ شرعية التطهير من النجاسات إنما لأداء الصلاة وما في حكمها. وإلى أنَّ الواجب إنَّما هو التطهير لمن يريد الصلاة، فأما خارج الصلاة فالتطهير ليس بفرض، فإنّه يجوزُ لبس الثوب النجس في غير الصلاة إلا إذا زادت النجاسة على قدر الدرهم، وله ثوب طاهر كما صرح به في «القنية»، وفي المقام تفصيل ذكرناه في شرح باب شروط الصلاة من «السعاية».
فإن قلت ما ذكره المصنف لوله هاهنا يغني عن قوله في «باب شروط الصلاة» : هي تطهير بدن المصلّي من حدث وخبث وثوبه ومكانه، فما وجه التكرار؟ قلت : لا غناء ولا تكرار، فإنّ المقصود هناك بيان أن طهارة البدن وغيره من الشرائط للصلاة، والغرض هاهنا مجرد وجوب تطهير البدن وغيره على المصلّي مع قطع النظر عن أن يكون فرضاً أو سنة، شرطاً أو ركناً.
أو نقول : المقصود هاهنا مجرَّدُ الإخبار عن كيفية التطهير وما يطهر به، والمقصود هناك خصوص كونه شرطاً. أو نقول : المراد بالمصلّي هاهنا المسلم لا من يريد الصلاة، وتخصيصه بالذكر ; لعدم كون الكافر مكلفاً بالفروع، لا سيما بتطهير الثياب والأبدان والأمكنة من النجاسات، أو لأنَّ المهتم بالشأن هو ذكر الأحكام المتعلقة بالمسلم والكافر تبع له. [١]قوله : وثوبه ومكانه ; ذكر في «الهداية» وغيرها : إنّ وجوب تطهير الثياب للمصلّى يثبت بقوله تعالى : وَثِيَابَكَ فَطَهِّرْ. تطهير البدن والمكان، وجوبه ثابت بدلالة النص. وفيه ما فيه، فإنّ وجوب تطهير البدن والمكان أيضاً دلّت عليه نصوص نبوية بعبارتها كما بسطناها في «السعاية»، فلا حاجة إلى إثباته بالدلالة. [٢]قوله : عن نجس ; هو بفتح الجيم بمعنى عين النجاسة، وهو على ضربين : مرئية، وغير مرئيّة، فالأوّل ما يبقى متجسدة ومنجمدة بعد الجفاف كالدم والغائط والمني، والثاني ما ليس كذلك ; كالبول. كذا في «العناية».
Chapter of Impurities. [1] His saying: 'yutahhar' (it is purified) — with the passive form from tathir, or with the active form from tahara. The ha (in yutahhiru) is fatha in the first and damma in the second. Although it is in the form of a report (khabar), it is a command in meaning, because in al-Nihaya: Verily the report of a mujtahid runs like the report of the Lawgiver in necessitating obligation; rather it is stronger than a command. So the meaning is: it is obligatory to purify the mentioned things from the mentioned impurities. And it is possible that the report is upon its literal meaning, and the purpose is to inform about what purifies things and how their purification is legislatively. [2] His saying: 'the body of the praying person' — what is meant by al-badan here is the torso (jasad), for it is stated in al-Mughrib and Majma‘ al-Bihar and others that al-badan (with two fatha) is a name for what is besides the head and limbs, and al-jasad is a name for the whole. And in its addition to 'the praying person' is an indication that the legislativity of purification from impurities is only for performing prayer and what is in its ruling. And that the obligatory is purification for the one who intends prayer; as for outside prayer, purification is not a command (fard), for it is permissible to wear a impure garment outside prayer unless the impurity exceeds the size of a dirham and he has a pure garment, as stated in al-Qunya. And in this place is a detail we mentioned in the commentary on the chapter of conditions of prayer from al-Si‘aya. If you say: What the author mentioned here would suffice over his saying in 'Chapter of Conditions of Prayer': 'It is purification of the body of the praying person from hadath and khabath, and his garment and his place.' So what is the face of repetition? I say: There is no sufficiency nor repetition — for the purpose there is to clarify that purification of the body and other things are conditions for prayer, and the aim here is merely the obligation of purification of the body and other things upon the praying person, disregarding whether it is fard or sunna, condition or pillar. Or we say: The purpose here is merely informing about the how of purification and what purifies with it, and the purpose there is specifically it being a condition. Or we say: What is meant by 'the praying person' here is the Muslim, not the one who intends prayer, and his specification in mention is because the disbeliever is not obligated with the branches, especially purification of garments, bodies, and places from impurities, or because the one concerned with the matter is mentioning rulings related to the Muslim while the disbeliever follows him. [1] His saying: 'and his garment and his place' — It is mentioned in al-Hidaya and others: Verily the obligation of purifying garments for the praying person is proven by His saying, Exalted: 'And your garments purify.' As for purification of the body and place, its obligation is established by indication of the text. There is something in it: For verily the obligation of purification of the body and place is also indicated by prophetic texts in their wording, as we have detailed in al-Si‘aya, so there is no need to establish it by indication. [2] His saying: 'from najas' — it is with fatha on the jim, meaning the substance of impurity. And it is of two types: visible and non-visible. The first is what remains embodied and congealed after drying, like blood, stool, and semen. The second is not like that, like urine. This is as in al-‘Inaya.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the text of al-Wiqaya concerning the chapter of impurities. The commentator begins by explaining the word 'yutahhar' (يطهر), noting that although it is in the form of a report, it functions as a command in meaning, as the mujtahid's statement carries the weight of obligation. The ruling is that the specified items must be purified from the specified impurities. Next, the commentator clarifies that 'badan' (بدن) here specifically refers to the torso (jasad), excluding the head and limbs, and that the phrase 'of the praying person' indicates that this obligation is connected to prayer: one must purify for prayer, but outside prayer, it is not obligatory unless the impurity exceeds a dirham's area and one has a clean garment available. The commentator then addresses a potential redundancy with the earlier statement in the chapter on conditions of prayer, explaining that the focus there was on purification as a condition (shart), while here the focus is on the obligation (wujub) itself. Alternatively, 'praying person' here may mean the Muslim in general, not just the one actively praying, as the disbeliever is not addressed in these rulings. The commentator then quotes al-Hidaya regarding the proof for purifying clothes: the Quranic verse 'And your garments purify' (74:4). For the body and place, some claim it is established by indication, but the commentator objects, stating that prophetic texts explicitly command purification of body and place as detailed in al-Si‘aya. Finally, the passage defines 'najas' (نجس) as the substance of impurity, dividing it into visible (مرئي) — which remains solid after drying, like blood, stool, and semen — and non-visible (غير مرئي), like urine. This categorization affects how purification is performed: visible impurities require removal of the substance, while non-visible may be purified by washing.

Key Terms
بدن (badan): In this passage, badan refers specifically to the torso (jasad), excluding the head and limbs, as opposed to jasad which means the whole body.
نجس مرئي (najas mar'i): A physically observable impurity that remains solid or congealed after drying, such as blood, stool, and semen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of a 'visible' impurity (najas mar'i)?
A) Any impurity that can be seen with the naked eye at any time.
B) An impurity that remains embodied and congealed after drying, like blood, stool, and semen.
C) An impurity that has a definite shape and color, like urine.
D) An impurity that is not liquid, such as dry dust.

Key Takeaway
Purification from visible impurity is wajib for prayer, with explicit proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and the obligation is tied to the intention to pray.

Taharah — Purification
