Minute Urine: Excused Due to Hardship
Exception for minute impurity based on hardship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a minute amount of urine and explain the reasoning based on hardship.

Core Idea
A tiny amount of urine (size of a needlehead) is excused to avoid hardship.

This lesson addresses a practical issue: small amounts of urine that are impossible to avoid completely. The Hanafi school excuses very small amounts, specifically comparing it to the head of a needle. This is based on the principle of removing hardship from the community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
The text says 'urine that splashes like the head of a needle is nothing' i.e., it does not nullify purity.
2
Understand the measure
The measure is the head of a needle. The commentary mentions that some scholars consider both sides of the needle, but to avoid hardship, it is excused.
3
Recognize the principle
The underlying principle is hardship (haraj) necessitates leniency. This is a minor concession in taharah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودمُ السمك ليس بنجس، ولعاب البغل، والحمار لا ينجس طاهراً، وبول انتضحَ مثل رؤوس الإبر ليس بشيء، وماءٌ وَرَدَ على نجس ، نجس كعكسه لا رماد قدر، وملح كان حماراً ودم السمك ليس بنجس، ولعاب البغل، والحمار لا ينجس طاهراً) ؛ لأنه مشكوك " ، فالطاهر لا تزول طهارته بالشَّكَ. (وبول انتضحَ مثل رؤوس الإبر ليس بشيء، وماءٌ وَرَدَ على نَجس، نجس كعكسه ) : أى كما أن الماءَ نَجَسٌ في عكسه، وهو ورود النجاسة على الماء. (لا رماد قدر ) ، وملح كان حماراً) : أي لا يكون شيء منهما نجساً ، وفي [١]قوله : ليس بنجس؛ لأنه ليس بدم حقيقة، بل رطوبة مائية شبيهة به، بدليل أن الدم إذا أصابته الشمس اسود ودم السمك يبيض. [٢]قوله : لأنه مشكوك ؛ يعني إذا أصاب الثوبَ والبدن لعاب البغل والحمار تجوزُ الصلاة به؛ لأنه مشكواً على ما مرَّ تحقيقه في «بحث السؤر ) ، والشك لا يزيلُ اليقين، فلا تزولُ به طهارة الثوب الثابتة باليقين. [٣] قوله : مثل رؤوس الإبر ؛ بكسر الهمزة وفتح الباء الموحدة، جمع الإبرة وهي : المخيط الذي ينظم فيه الخيط، ويخاط به الثوب ، يقال له بالفارسية : سوزن ، والتقييد بالرأس يفيد أنه لو أصابه بقدر الجانب الآخر يلزمُ غسله، ومن المشايخ من قال : لا يعتبر الجانبان ؛ دفعاً للحرج. كذا في «فتح القدير» [٤] قوله : وماء ورد ؛ مبتدأ خبره نجس الثاني وهو بكسر الجيم ، والأول بفتحها، ويجوز الكسر فيهما ، يعني ما جرى على شيءٍ نجس أو نجاسة نجس ، كما أنّ الماء الوارد عليه النجس نجس ؛ لوجود الاختلاط بالنجاسة. [0] قوله : لا رماد ؛ أي رماد القذر ليس بنجس، وكذا ملح كان حماراً أو غيره من الحيوانات، فوقع في المملحة ، فانقلب ملحا طاهر، بشرط أن لا يكون نجس العين، وذلك لأن انقلاب العين يزيل وصف النجاسة، فإنّ زوال الذات مستلزم لزوال الوصف. (۱) المراد به العذرة والروث. ينظر : (رد المحتار» (۱ : ۲۱۷). (۲) (ص۲۰۹ - ۲۱۰). (۳) «فتح القدير (۱) : (۲۰۹) ، وينظر : تبيين الحقائق (۱) : (۷۵) ، و (مجمع الأنهر» (١: ٦٣). وينظر: «التنبيه»(۱ : ۱۷)، و(المنهاج وشرحه (مغني المحتاج (۱): ۸۱)، فإن عبارتها تدل على خلاف الشافعي في مسألة رماد القذر، ومسألة ملح كان حماراً ؛ لأنه لا يطهر نجس العين عندهم إلا خمر تخللت خمراً وجلداً نجس بالموت فيطهر بدبغه.
Fish blood is not impure, and the saliva of the mule and donkey does not make a pure thing impure. And urine that splashes like the head of a needle is nothing. And water that comes upon impurity becomes impure, like its opposite. Not ash of a stove, and salt that was from a donkey. And fish blood is not impure, and the saliva of the mule and donkey does not make a pure thing impure; because it is doubtful, and the pure does not lose its purity by doubt. (And urine that splashes like the head of a needle is nothing, and water that comes upon impurity becomes impure like its opposite): meaning just as the water is impure in its opposite, which is the coming of impurity upon water. (Not ash of a stove, and salt that was from a donkey): meaning none of them is impure. And in [1] his saying: not impure; because it is not real blood, but a watery moisture resembling it, as evidence that when blood is exposed to the sun it blackens, while fish blood whitens. [2] His saying: because it is doubtful; meaning if the saliva of the mule or donkey touches the garment or body, it is permissible to pray with it; because it is doubtful as previously detailed in the 'discussion of remnants', and doubt does not remove certainty, so the purity of the garment established with certainty is not removed by it. [3] His saying: like the heads of needles; with kasra of the hamza and fatha of the ba, plural of needle, which is the sewing tool through which thread is passed and with which cloth is sewn, called in Persian 'suzan'. The qualification with the head indicates that if it touches to the extent of the other side, washing becomes obligatory. And some mashayikh said: both sides are not considered, to avoid hardship. So in Fath al-Qadir. [4] His saying: water that comes; subject whose predicate is the second 'najis' with kasr of the jim, and the first with fatha, and it is permissible to have kasra on both. Meaning what flows over something impure or impurity becomes impure, just as water upon which impurity falls is impure due to the existence of mixing with impurity. [0] His saying: not ash; meaning the ash of filth is not impure, and likewise salt that was from a donkey or other animals, that falls into the salt cellar and turns into salt is pure, provided that it is not an impure substance itself, because the transformation of substance removes the description of impurity, for the removal of the essence necessitates the removal of the description. (1) By it is meant filth and dung. See: Radd al-Muhtar 1:217. (2) pp. 209-210. (3) Fath al-Qadir 1:209, and see: Tabyin al-Haqaiq 1:75, and Majma' al-Anhur 1:63. And see: al-Tanbih 1:17, and al-Minhaj and its explanation (Mughni al-Muhtaj 1:81), for their expressions indicate the difference of al-Shafi'i regarding the issue of ash of filth and the issue of salt that was from a donkey; because an impure substance is not purified in their school except wine that turns into vinegar, and skin that is najis due to death that is purified by tanning.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This commentary explains several rulings on impurities. Fish blood is not impure because it is not real blood; proof is that it whitens in the sun whereas true blood blackens. Saliva of mules and donkeys is doubtful, so it does not remove the certainty of purity. A tiny amount of urine (size of a needle head) is excused due to hardship. Water becomes impure when it contacts impurity, whether the impurity is solid or liquid. However, ash from burnt filth and salt that has transformed from animal origin are pure because the essence changed. The Hanafi position on transformation differs from the Shafi'i school, which only allows purification through transformation for wine into vinegar and tanned skin.

Key Terms
رؤوس الإبر (ru'us al-ibar): Heads of needles; a measure for excusable impurity.
الحرج (al-haraj): Hardship; a reason for leniency in rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum amount of urine that is excused in the Hanafi school?
A) The size of a pea
B) The size of a needlehead
C) The amount that cannot be avoided
D) Any amount less than a drop

Key Takeaway
A minute amount of urine (size of a needlehead) is excused to avoid hardship.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
5 min
Water That Meets Impurity: The Mixing Rule
Ruling on water that contacts impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why water becomes impure when it contacts impurity, and identify the ruling is the same whether the water falls on impurity or impurity falls into water.

Core Idea
Water becomes impure when it mixes with impurity, regardless of which moves first.

This lesson covers a fundamental rule of taharah: water that comes into contact with an impurity becomes impure itself. The text emphasizes that the ruling is symmetrical—whether water flows over impurity or impurity falls into water, the result is the same: the water becomes najis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The text states 'water that comes upon impurity becomes impure, like its opposite'.
2
Understand the symmetry
'Like its opposite' means the same ruling applies if impurity comes upon water.
3
Apply the condition
The water becomes impure due to mixing (ikhtilat). The degree of mixing is what matters, not the direction.

Source Text

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Transformation (Inqilab al-‘Ayn): Ash and Salt Become Pure
Ruling based on transformation principle with cross-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of transformation (inqilab al-‘ayn) to determine the purity of ash and salt, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
When a substance's essence changes entirely, it becomes pure—even if it came from an impure source.

This lesson tackles the important principle of transformation. Ash from burnt filth and salt that was once part of a donkey are ruled pure because their entire substance changed. This contrasts with the Shafi'i school, which allows purification by transformation only in specific cases like wine becoming vinegar. Understanding this principle is key to many rulings in taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items
The text mentions ash (ramad) and salt (milh) that came from impure sources.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
Both are pure because their essence has transformed.
3
Understand the principle
Transformation (inqilab al-‘ayn) removes impurity. The removal of the original substance necessitates removal of its attribute.
4
Note the condition
This applies only if the original matter was not an intrinsically impure substance (najis al-‘ayn) itself. Ash from pork bones? Actually, the condition is that the transformed substance is not originally an impure substance; the source text says 'provided that it is not an impure substance itself'.
Careful: 'najis al-ayn' is intrinsic impurity; if the original material was inherently impure (like wine), transformation may not suffice in some cases.
5
Compare with Shafi'i
The Shafi'i school restricts transformation to wine into vinegar and skin tanning. For ash and salt, they remain impure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) By it is meant filth and dung. See: Radd al-Muhtar 1:217. (2) pp. 209-210. (3) Fath al-Qadir 1:209, and see: Tabyin al-Haqaiq 1:75, and Majma' al-Anhur 1:63. And see: al-Tanbih 1:17, and al-Minhaj and its explanation (Mughni al-Muhtaj 1:81), for their expressions indicate the difference of al-Shafi'i regarding the issue of ash of filth and the issue of salt that was from a donkey; because an impure substance is not purified in their school except wine that turns into vinegar, and skin that is najis due to death that is purified by tanning.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This commentary explains several rulings on impurities. Fish blood is not impure because it is not real blood; proof is that it whitens in the sun whereas true blood blackens. Saliva of mules and donkeys is doubtful, so it does not remove the certainty of purity. A tiny amount of urine (size of a needle head) is excused due to hardship. Water becomes impure when it contacts impurity, whether the impurity is solid or liquid. However, ash from burnt filth and salt that has transformed from animal origin are pure because the essence changed. The Hanafi position on transformation differs from the Shafi'i school, which only allows purification through transformation for wine into vinegar and tanned skin.

Key Terms
انقلاب العين (inqilab al-ayn): The transformation of the substance of an object, causing removal of impurity.
نجس العين (najis al-ayn): An object intrinsically impure (e.g., blood, pork).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is ash from burnt dung pure?
A) Because fire destroys all impurity
B) Because the essence of the dung has transformed into a different substance
C) Because dung is not impure
D) Because the ash is very small in quantity

Key Takeaway
Complete transformation of essence removes impurity, provided the original substance was not intrinsically impure.

Prayer on Garments and Mats with Impure Parts: Conditions for Validity
Commentator expands on conditions for prayer on impure-lined garments and impure-edged mats.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which prayer is valid on a garment or mat with an impure part, and apply the Hanafi ruling to distinguish between connected and separate impure areas.

Core Idea
Prayer is valid on a pure side if it is effectively separate from impurity.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies that impurity on part of your garment or mat does not automatically invalidate prayer. The key is whether the impure part is considered separate or connected. Let's examine three scenarios: lining, mat edge, and dampness from a wet cloth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three cases: garment with impure lining, mat with impure end, and pure garment showing dampness from wrapped wet impure cloth.
Each has a different condition for validity.
2
Determine the condition for each
For lining: the garment must not be sewn (mudarrab). For mat: the ends must not move together (i.e., mat is large). For dampness: no moisture transfer (like dripping).
3
Understand the underlying principle
The pure part must be effectively separate from the impurity. Physical connection (sewing, small mat size) or moisture transfer makes them one unit, invalidating prayer.
4
Apply to a new case
Consider a large prayer rug with a small stain on one corner. Since moving the stain does not move the whole rug, the clean area is separate and prayer is valid.
If the rug is small and shakes entirely, the whole rug is considered one unit and prayer is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلى على ثوب بطانته نجس وعلى طرف بساط طرف آخر منه نجس يتحرك أحدهما بتحريك الآخر أو لا وفي ثوب ظهر فيه ندوة ثوب رطب نجس لف فيه لا كما يقطر شيء لو. ويصلى على ثوب بطانته نجس) أي إذا لم يكن الثوب مضرًّا. (وعلى طرف بساط طرف آخر منه نجس يتحرك أحدهما بتحريك الآخر أو لا)، وإنما قال هذا احترازاً عن قول من قال إنما تجوز الصلاة على الطرف الآخر إذا لم يتحرك أحد الطرفين بتحريك الآخر. (وفي ثوب ظهر فيه ندوة ثوب رطب نجس لف فيه، لا كما يقطر شيء) [١]قوله بطانته بكسر الأول هو الطرف الداخل من الثوب يعني إذا كان ذا وجهين أحدهما نجس ففرشه على الأرض وصلى على الطاهر جاز لأنه بالانفصال صار في حكم الثوب الآخر بخلاف ما إذا كان أحدهما مخيطاً بالآخر فإنه في حكم شيء واحد. [٢] قوله إذا لم يتحرك ... الخ فإنه إذا تحرك بأن كان صغيراً صار الطرفان في حكم شيء واحد فكأنه صلى على نجس ومن لم يقيد به استند بأن البساط كالأرض حكم واحد فتشترط فيه طهارة مكان الصلاة فحسب ولا يقدح فيه نجاسة الطرف الآخر. [٣] قوله لف ضمير الفعل المجهول إلى الثوب الأول الطاهر وضمير فيه إلى الثوب الرطب النجس. (٢) الثوب مضراً أي مخيطاً. ينظر: «اللسان» (٤ : ٢٥٧٠). (٣) سواء كان كبيراً أو صغيراً لأنه بمنزلة الأرض فيشترط فيه طهارة موضع الصلاة فقيد الطرف اتفاقي. ينظر: فتح باب العناية) (١ : ٢٦٢). (٤) ندوة بلة. ينظر: «مختار» (ص ٦٥٣).
And he may pray on a garment whose lining is impure, and on one side of a mat whose other side is impure, whether one side moves when the other moves or not, and in a garment that shows dampness from a wet impure cloth wrapped in it, he may not pray, just as if something were to drip. And he may pray on a garment whose lining is impure) meaning if the garment is not stitched together. (And on one side of a mat whose other side is impure, whether one side moves when the other moves or not), and he only said this as a precaution against the statement of one who says: prayer on the other side is only permissible if one side does not move when the other moves. (And in a garment that shows dampness from a wet impure cloth wrapped in it, he may not pray, just as if something were to drip). [1] His saying: its lining; with kasra of the first, it is the inner side of the garment. Meaning if the garment has two sides, one of which is impure, and he spreads it on the ground and prays on the pure side, it is permissible because by separation it becomes like a different garment. But if one side is sewn to the other, it is considered one thing. [2] His saying: when it does not move... etc; for if it moves, as when it is small, the two sides become like one thing, so it is as if he prayed on impurity. Those who do not qualify rely on the fact that the mat is like the ground, a single entity, so only the purity of the place of prayer is required, and impurity of the other side does not harm. [3] His saying: wrapped; the pronoun of the passive verb refers to the first pure garment, and the pronoun 'in it' refers to the wet impure cloth. (2) The garment is sewn; meaning stitched. See: Lisan al-'Arab 4:2570. (3) Whether large or small; because it is like the ground, so only the purity of the place of prayer is required, and the qualification of the side is incidental. See: Fath Bab al-'Inaya 1:262. (4) Dampness: wetness. See: Mukhtar p.653.
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This passage discusses when prayer is valid despite impurity on a garment or mat. If a garment has two separate sides (not sewn), one impure, one can spread it and pray on the pure side. But if the sides are sewn together, they are considered one garment and prayer is not valid. For a mat, if the two ends move together (small mat) then prayer is invalid on the pure end; if they do not move together (large mat), the pure end is separate and prayer is valid. If a wet impure cloth is wrapped in a pure garment and moisture appears on the pure garment (dampness), prayer is not valid if the moisture transfers; but if only a trace without dripping, it may be excused.

Key Terms
بطانة (biṭānah): The inner side or lining of a garment.
مُضَرَّب (muḍarrab): A garment whose sides are stitched together, making it a single entity.
ندوة (nadwah): Dampness or wetness that appears on a garment from another wet object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is prayer valid on one end of a mat if the other end is impure?
A) Only if the mat is large and the ends do not move together
B) Only if the mat is small and the ends do not move together
C) Only if the mat is large and the ends move together
D) It is always valid

Key Takeaway
Impurity on a garment or mat does not invalidate prayer if the pure part is effectively separate and no moisture transfers.

Prayer on a Garment with Najis Inner Lining
States ruling on impurity in garment lining

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying on a garment with a najis inner lining and identify the key condition that determines validity.

Core Idea
A najis lining invalidates prayer only if it is sewn; if separate, the pure side is like a clean garment.

This lesson examines a specific case from the chapter of impurities: when can you pray on a garment whose inner lining is najis? The ruling hinges on a single physical detail—whether the lining is sewn to the outer layer. Understanding this condition helps avoid invalid prayer due to hidden impurity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying on a garment whose inner lining (bitanah) is najis. The general ruling: prayer is valid, but with an important condition.
The default is permissibility unless the condition is violated.
2
Understand the key term 'bitanah'
Bitanah refers to the inner lining, the side that faces the body. It is distinct from the outer face. In this context, it is a separate piece of fabric that may or may not be sewn.
The text uses a specific term; do not confuse with 'battanah' (inner side of a single-layer garment).
3
Recognize the condition: not sewn (ghayr mudarrab)
The text says the ruling applies 'if the garment is not mudarrab' (i.e., the lining is not sewn to the outer layer). When the lining is separate, the pure part is considered a separate garment.
Mudarrab means sewn, stitched together.
4
Differentiate the sewn case
If the lining is sewn to the outer layer, the two parts are one unit. In that case, the impurity is considered attached, and prayer on any part is invalid.
This is an exception: the ruling flips from valid to invalid.
5
Apply the reasoning: separation creates a new ruling
The underlying principle: when the pure part is physically separate (not sewn), it is treated as a distinct garment. The impurity in the lining does not transfer because it is a separate piece.
This is a pragmatic ruling that facilitates ease in purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُصَلِّي على ثوب بطانته نجس) : أي إذا لم يكن الثَّوبُ مُضَرَّباً. [1] قوله : بطانته ؛ بكسر الأوّل هو الطرف الداخلُ من الثوب، يعني إذا كان ذا وجهين أحدهما نجس ففرشه على الأرض وصلى على الطاهر جاز؛ لأنه بالانفصال صار في حكم الثوب الآخر، بخلاف ما إذا كان أحدهما مخيطاً بالآخر، فإنّه في حكم شيء واحد. (2) الثوب مُضَرَّباً : أي مخيطاً. ينظر: «اللسان»(٤ : ٢٥٧٠).
He prays on a garment whose inner lining is najis: that is, if the garment is not sewn (mudarrab). [1] Explanation: 'Bitanah' is the inner side of the garment. If it has two sides, one of which is najis, and he spreads it on the ground and prays on the pure side, it is permissible, because due to separation it becomes in the ruling of another garment, contrary to if one is sewn to the other, then it is in the ruling of one thing. (2) 'Mudarrab': sewn. See: al-Lisan (4:2570).
Source pages p. 559

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter of impurities. The text permits prayer on a garment whose inner lining is najis, provided the lining is not sewn (mudarrab) to the outer part. If sewn, the two are considered one unit and prayer is invalid. The reasoning is that when not sewn, the pure part is like a separate garment. This is a standard Hanafi position, as the lining is not attached.

Key Terms
بطانة (bitanah): The inner lining of a garment, opposite of outer face.
مضرب (mudarrab): Sewn, stitched together; here refers to the lining being sewn to the outer layer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is prayer valid on a garment with a najis inner lining?
A) Always valid
B) Only if the lining is sewn
C) Only if the lining is not sewn
D) Never valid

Key Takeaway
Prayer on a garment with a najis inner lining is valid only if the lining is not sewn to the outer part, because separation makes the pure part like a separate garment.
